          (INTO THE FUTURE)

The sun was shining brightly as the new students of Nightshade Wonderland gathered in the courtyard. Lilith, a senior with striking features and an enchanting smile, stood before them.

"You are all welcomed to our school," Lilith said, her voice warm and inviting. "I'm sure you're going to love it here."

The new students exchanged excited glances, their eyes sparkling with anticipation. One of them, a timid-looking girl with curly brown hair, raised her hand.

"What should we expect from here?" she asked, her voice barely above a whisper.

Lilith's smile broadened. "A lot of fun and trouble," she said, her eyes glinting with mischief. "Let's just say some of you will have fun, and some will be...unlucky."

The new students laughed nervously, unsure what to make of Lilith's enigmatic warning.

Arachne, a petite girl with butterfly flying around her, raised her hand next. 

"Can you tell us the history of the school?" she asked.

Lilith nodded, a faraway look in her eyes. "Nightshade Wonderland was founded thousands of years ago," she began. "It was founded by Master Nox, a powerful sorcerer who sought to create a haven for magical beings."

As Lilith spoke, the air around her began to shimmer and shine. The new students gasped in wonder as images began to appear in the air, illustrating Lilith's words.

They saw Master Nox, a tall, imposing figure with piercing eyes, standing before a grand, sprawling castle. They saw his son, a young man with a mischievous grin, taking over the school after Master Nox's death.

And they saw Mistress Morwen, a stately woman with long, flowing hair, taking the reins after Master Darko's passing.

"I hear Mistress Morwen has two daughters," Arachne said, her eyes sparkling with interest.

Lilith's smile faltered for a moment, before she regained her composure. 

"Yes, that's true," she said.

 "Maledicta and Benedicta. I would really advise you all to stay away from the first one...if you love your life." She warned.

The new students exchanged nervous glances, unsure what to make of Lilith's warning.

But before they could ask any more questions, a commotion broke out at the edge of the courtyard, students were running away, their faces pale and frightened.

"What's going on?" one of the new students asked, alarm rising in her voice.

Lilith's eyes flicked towards the disturbance, before she turned back to the new students. 

"Just hide for now," she said, her voice low and urgent.

The new students didn't need to be told twice. They scattered, hiding behind nearby statues or darting into the nearby buildings.

Arachne stood frozen, unsure what to do. But before she could move, Lilith grabbed her arm and pulled her into a nearby alcove.

"Don't speak," Lilith whispered, her eyes fixed on something across the courtyard. "Just watch."

Arachne peeked around the edge of the alcove, her heart pounding in her chest. And then she saw her.

Maledicta, Mistress Morwen's daughter, was walking across the courtyard, her eyes fixed on some point in the distance, her white hair reaching her waist. Her aura was like nothing Arachne had ever seen before - cold, chilling, and utterly terrifying.

People were running away from her, their faces pale and frightened. And Arachne could see why. Maledicta's very presence seemed to draw the light out of the air, leaving only darkness and shadow in her wake.

"That's Maledicta," Lilith whispered, her voice barely audible. "The daughter of Mistress Morwen. She's cursed, and a glare from her can send you to the ground. And that dark shadow looming around her...that's doom."

Arachne felt a shiver run down her spine as she watched Maledicta walk away. She couldn't help but feel a twinge of pity for the girl, who seemed so alone and isolated.

"I don't think she's that bad, though," Arachne said, her voice barely above a whisper.

Lilith raised an eyebrow, a hint of surprise in her eyes. 

"You will get your answer soon," she said, before turning and disappearing into the crowd.

Arachne watched her go, before turning back to gaze across the courtyard. Maledicta was still walking away, her dark shadow looming behind her like a specter of doom.

The stone shattered into a thousand pieces as Maledicta's presence washed over it. The demons surrounding the stone's holder let out a collective shriek as they began to burn, their bodies dissolving into ash as they stumbled and fell.

As he waited for the ambulance to arrive, he couldn't shake the feeling that he had just stumbled into something much bigger than himself.

Kaiden paced anxiously outside the hospital room, his mind racing with worst-case scenarios. He had found her lying on the cat, bleeding profusely, and his heart had almost stopped. Who was she? And what had happened to her?

The doctor emerged from the room, a reassuring smile on his face.

 "How is she, doctor?" Kaiden asked worriedly.

"Nothing is wrong, she's just stressed," the doctor said, his expression calm.

(A STUDENT AT NIGHTSHADE WONDERLAND)

Kaiden's eyes blazed with anger as he yelled after Maledicta. 

"Hey, hey, hey, hey girl! You can't bring me to this strange place without my permission and suddenly tell me it's my new home!" He yelled.

But Maledicta didn't even flinch. She just kept walking, her long white hair swaying behind her.

Kaiden's frustration boiled over, and he grabbed her arm, spinning her around to face him. 

"You didn't even let me know the type of place this was," he yelled. "What if it's dangerous?"

Maledicta's eyes flashed with anger, and she jerked her arm free. 

"Don't ever touch me again," she said coldly, her voice dripping with venom.

"Sorry, I did;n't mean to‚Äî"

But Maledicta was already walking away, leaving Kaiden standing alone in the middle of the courtyard.

That's when Kaiden finally noticed the pool of people staring at him. They were all dressed in strange, elaborate clothing, and their eyes seemed to be boring into his soul.

"Is he a human?" one of them asked, their voice full of curiosity.

"I don't know, I haven't seen one before," another one replied. "I just read about them."

"He looks strange, though," a third one added, their eyes narrowing as they glared at Kaiden.

Kaiden stood frozen, unsure of what to do. They all seemed to be mad at him, and he had no idea why.

He took a deep breath and decided to walk around, trying to get a feel for the place. As he strolled through the courtyard, he noticed that everyone seemed to be staring at him.

He saw a girl who suddenly vanished into thin air, and another person who was flying through the air with ease. Kaiden's eyes widened as he realized that these people were not normal.

They were all...magical.

Kaiden's mind reeled as he tried to process what he was seeing. He had always thought of himself as a rational person, but this place was challenging everything he thought he knew.

As he walked, Kaiden noticed that the buildings around him seemed to be shifting and changing. The walls seemed to be made of a strange, glowing material, and the windows seemed to be staring back at him like empty eyes.

Kaiden's skin crawled as he realized that he was completely out of his depth. He had no idea what this place was, or what its inhabitants wanted from him.

All he knew was that he wanted to get out of there as fast as he could.

But as he turned to leave, Kaiden realized that he had no idea where he was going. The courtyard seemed to be shifting and changing around him, and he couldn't see any exits.

He was trapped.

And then, Kaiden heard a voice behind him. 

"Welcome to Nightshade Wonderland," it said. 

"You're going to be here for a while.‚Äù the voice added. He look around but found nothing, he was a little terrified but he didn't even know who to approach among the strange people.

           QUEEN EPUSA COVEN

The Queen Epusa Coven was a place of darkness and foreboding, where the very air seemed to vibrate with malevolent energy. The demons that inhabited this realm moved with an unnatural gait, their twisted forms seeming to shift and writhe like living shadows.

At the center of this dark coven stood a throne, upon which sat the queen herself. Epusa was a woman of imposing presence, her two curved horns gleaming with a sickly, yellowish light. Her black gown seemed to absorb the faint illumination that filtered through the coven, making her appear almost like a void incarnate.

Snakes slithered and curled around her body, their forked tongues darting in and out of their mouths as they seemed to sense the dark energy that emanated from their mistress.

A figure entered the coven, bowing its head in a gesture of abject submission. 

"Did you find him?" Epusa asked, her voice low and menacing.

The figure trembled, its voice barely above a whisper. "I...I couldn't, my queen."

Epusa's expression turned icy, her eyes flashing with anger. 

"What? You couldn't?" she yelled, her voice like a crack of thunder. The wind seemed to respond to her fury, picking up and sending several demons tumbling through the air.

The figure cowered, its eyes fixed on the ground.

 "I am sorry, my queen. Maledicta suddenly showed up and ruined everything." He said.

Epusa's gaze narrowed, her eyes burning with intensity. 

"That girl came to the future?" she asked, her voice dripping with malice.

The figure nodded, still trembling.

 "Yes, my queen. But I think she is dead. I stabbed her twice with a dagger poisoned with blackthorn juice." He said.

Epusa's expression turned skeptical. 

"Where is her body?" she asked, her voice cold.

The figure hesitated, its eyes darting around the coven as if searching for an escape route.

 "I...I couldn't find it, my queen. She must be dead somewhere." He said nervously.

Epusa's laughter was like a cold wind, sending shivers down the spines of the demons that cowered around her. 

"You are really foolish to think that girl is dead," she said, her voice dripping with contempt. "You don't know the type of person she is."

The figure took a step back, its eyes wide with fear. 

"She can't survive the stab to her chest," he protested.

Epusa's expression turned glacial.

 "If you can't get him, then where is the stone I gave you?" she asked, her voice like a knife cutting through the air.

The figure hesitated, its eyes dropping to the ground.

 "It was destroyed when Maledicta showed up," it mumbled.

Epusa's scream was like a crack of thunder, shaking the very foundations of the coven.

 "What!!" she yelled, springing up from her throne. "The stone I used all my energy to build, how dare you!"

The figure cowered, its eyes fixed on the ground as Epusa's snakes slithered towards it, their forked tongues darting in and out of their mouths.

But before the snakes could strike, Maledicta suddenly appeared in their midst, her eyes blazing with fury. The demons nearby scurried for cover, hiding themselves from her wrath.

The snakes that had been approaching the figure suddenly burst into flames, their ashes drifting to the groung.

    ‚ÄúHow dare you came into my place without my permission‚Äù Epusa yelled angrily. Maledicta ignored Epusa's furious gaze and strode towards the cowering figure.

With a swift, deadly motion, she stabbed the figure straight in the chest. And then, just as suddenly, she vanished into thin air.

Epusa's eyes blazed with fury as she watched her demon melt into a puddle of goo. 

"That witch, I will kill her," she snarled, her voice like a rusty gate.

She knew she had to do something fast and stop the girl before she turn to something else.

And with that thought, Benedicta drifted off to sleep.

Ryder's expression turned thoughtful, but before he could respond, a commotion at the door caught his attention.

Ryder didn't respond, his eyes fixed on the Arachne, who has a nervous smile on her face.

Arachne's eyes were fixed on the floor, her face pale. But as she looked up, her eyes met Ryder's, and her expression changed from nervousness to shock.

"You......" she started to say, her voice trailing off.

Ryder's expression remained neutral, but his eyes seemed to bore into Arachne's soul.

"Do you know each other?" the king asked, his voice curious.

"No, I don't know her."Ryder spoke up quickly, his voice firm.

Arachne's eyes flashed with surprise, and she looked like she was about to say something. But Ryder's expression silenced her, and she looked away, her face pale.

Ryder stood up, his eyes fixed on Arachne. "Follow me." He muttered.

He turned and walked away, leaving Arachne to follow him. She looked back at her parents, who gave her an encouraging smile. She bow to the king and queen.

The room fell silent, and the king smiled, "Well, I suppose we'll just have to wait and see." He said.

It was a rare day off for the students, and the counpound was filled with the sound of laughter and idle chatter. Some students were lounging in the sun, while others were engaged in lively games of tag or hide-and-seek.

But amidst all the revelry, two figures were seen sneaking out of the school. They moved stealthily, trying not to draw attention to themselves as they made their way towards the back gate.

Once they were outside, they quickened their pace, trekking through the dense forest that surrounded the school. The trees seemed to close in around them, casting deep shadows that made it difficult to see.

But the two figures pressed on, their eyes fixed on some point in the distance. Finally, after what seemed like an eternity, they emerged into a small clearing. In the center of the clearing stood an old, dilapidated house, its walls cracked and weathered with age.

Aka, one of the two figures, made a move to vanish into the house, but Ryder, the other figure, quickly caught her arm. 

"You can't vanish into my grandfather's house," he whispered urgently.

Aka nodded, and Ryder carefully reset the trap. He made another book appear, identical to the one Aka had taken, before closing the door.

As he turned to leave, he realized that Aka was nowhere to be seen. He quickly walked outside, his heart racing with anxiety. His grandfather was starting to stir, and Ryder knew they had to get out of there fast.

He took off after Aka, to catch up to her and retrieve the book.

Aka shrugged, her eyes scanning the page. She had always been one to disregard warnings, and this was no exception.

She began to read, her eyes widening as she delved deeper into the book. The story was five hundred years old, dating back to the time when Mistress Morwen had just taken over the school from her father.

A strange man had appeared at the school, charming and charismatic. His name was Damian, and Aka's eyes widened as she realized that this was her father.

She continued reading, her eyes growing wider in shock. Her father had come to the school because he had heard about the prophecy of the child Lucan, who would give the demons the strength to take over the world.

The school had been unaware of Damian's true intentions. He had almost ended the students, using them as sacrifices to his dark god. Aka's mind reeled as she read the words, her heart pounding in her chest.

"My father isn't like that," she whispered, shaking her head in shock. "That's not my father."

But the words on the page didn't lie. Damian had been found out, performing his dark ritual in secret. The goddess had cursed him, but he had taken his own life before the curse could take effect.

The curse had then passed to one of his children, and Aka's eyes widened as she realized that this must be why her mother had always been so secretive about her past.

It was only after Damian's death that it was discovered that Mistress Morwen was pregnant with his children. Aka's mind reeled as she realized the implications.

Did that mean...? Could it be...?

The book fell from Aka's hand, her eyes widening in shock. Maledicta and Benedicta were her younger sisters.

The room spun around her, Aka's mind racing with thoughts. Her mother had lied to her about her father's death. Epusa had told her that he had been killed while out hunting, but it seemed that was just a cover story.

Aka stood up, her heart pounding in her chest. She couldn't believe the truth. She had always thought of Maledicta and Benedicta as her enemies, but now...now she wasn't so sure.

She walked back to the book, her eyes scanning the pages once more. There had to be more to the story, more secrets hidden within the pages.

As she read on, Aka's mind reeled with the implications. She was related to the sisters, and her father's past was far darker than she had ever imagined.

The room grew darker, the shadows deepening as Aka delved deeper into the book. She was uncovering secrets that were meant to remain hidden, secrets that could change everything.

       FEW HOURS LATER

Aka stood in front of the book, her eyes scanning the pages with a mixture of shock and disbelief. She had just finished reading the entire book, and what she had discovered was almost too much to bear.

According to the book, Aka was connected to Maledicta in ways she never could have imagined. They shared the same blood, and that made Aka a potential weakness for Maledicta. It was all part of the curse that had been placed upon Maledicta.

But Aka didn't want to believe any of it. She was only going to believe what her mother had told her.

She was stunned. This meant that Maledicta and Benedicta were her sisters, connected to her by blood.

‚ÄúI can't. She has to be useful to me. She hasn't been able to achieve anything she promised to do. She couldn't even bring the blood of that girl to me. She's useless, just like her father."Epusa said.
